<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Return of capital to shareholders was $1.2&nbsp;billion </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Announced agreement to acquire Ricolino, Mexico&#146;s leading confectionery company with iconic brands and
strong distribution capabilities, doubling the size of our Mexico business </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Appointed Mariano Lozano to the role of EVP and President, Latin America </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">CHICAGO, Ill. &#150; April&nbsp;26, 2022 &#150; Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (Nasdaq: MDLZ) today reported its first quarter 2022
results. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;We delivered strong <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">top-line</FONT> results in our first quarter, driven by higher
pricing and strong volume growth. Our chocolate and biscuit businesses continue to power our virtuous cycle of attractive revenue growth, strong profitability and robust cash flow,&#148; said Dirk Van de Put, Chairman and Chief Executive Officer.
&#147;Demand remains strong across both developed and emerging markets, with all our regions posting growth. We expect elevated levels of input cost inflation to continue through the remainder of the year, and we will continue to take necessary
actions to offset this dynamic - including a broader revenue growth management agenda, ongoing cost discipline, and further simplification within our business. We remain confident in our strategy and ability to create long-term value, while
recognizing the need to stay agile to navigate the dynamic economic and geopolitical environment. We are also excited about our recently announced agreement to acquire Ricolino that will step-change our presence in the priority market of Mexico
&#151; adding to our portfolio some of the country&#146;s most beloved chocolate and candy brands, while broadening our distribution footprint with more than 2,100 direct store delivery routes reaching 440,000 traditional trade outlets.&#148; </P>
</DIV></Center>

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><U>First Quarter Commentary </U></I></P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Net revenues</B> increased 7.3&nbsp;percent driven by Organic Net Revenue growth of 8.6&nbsp;percent, and
incremental sales from the company&#146;s acquisitions of Chipita, Grenade and Gourmet Food, partially offset by unfavorable currency. Pricing and volume drove Organic Net Revenue growth. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Gross profit </B>increased $17&nbsp;million, while gross profit margin decreased 260 basis points to
38.4&nbsp;percent primarily driven by lower <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> gains from derivatives, the decrease in Adjusted Gross
Profit<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP> margin and incremental costs incurred due to the war in Ukraine. Adjusted Gross Profit increased $283&nbsp;million at constant currency, while Adjusted Gross Profit margin decreased 80
basis points to 38.8&nbsp;percent due to higher raw material and transportation costs and unfavorable mix, partially offset by pricing, productivity and volume leverage. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Operating income </B>decreased $189&nbsp;million and operating income margin was 14.1&nbsp;percent, down 360
basis points primarily due to incremental costs incurred due to the war in Ukraine, lower <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> gains from derivatives, intangible asset impairment charges
incurred in 2022, higher acquisition integration costs and lower Adjusted Operating Income<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP> margin, partially offset by lower restructuring costs. Adjusted Operating Income increased
$175&nbsp;million at constant currency while Adjusted Operating Income margin decreased 20 basis points to 17.7&nbsp;percent, with input cost inflation and unfavorable mix, mostly offset by pricing and SG&amp;A leverage. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Diluted EPS</B> was $0.61, down 10.3&nbsp;percent, primarily due to incremental costs incurred due to the war
in Ukraine, lower <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> gains from derivatives, intangible asset impairment charges incurred in 2022 and higher acquisition-related costs, partially offset by
an increase in Adjusted EPS and lower restructuring costs. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

interest expense and fewer shares outstanding, partially offset by higher taxes primarily due to lower net benefits from <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-recurring</FONT> discrete tax items and lower benefit plan
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-service</FONT> income. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>2022 Outlook </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International provides its outlook on a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> basis, as the company cannot predict
some elements that are included in reported GAAP results, including the impact of foreign exchange. Refer to the Outlook section in the discussion of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures below for more details. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company is updating its fiscal 2022 outlook to reflect expectations for continued <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">top-line</FONT> growth,
higher cost of goods sold inflation, the timing effect of additional pricing actions and the impact of the war in Ukraine. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For 2022, the
company now expects 4+ percent Organic Net Revenue growth, which reflects the strength of its first quarter and higher pricing related to increased input costs. The company also now expects <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mid-to-high</FONT></FONT> single digit Adjusted EPS growth on a constant currency basis due to the current estimates of the loss of earnings from the war in Ukraine and material commodity cost increases due primarily to
increases in energy costs. The company&#146;s Free Cash Flow outlook remains at $3+ billion. The company estimates currency translation would decrease 2022 net revenue growth by approximately 3
percent<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">3</SUP> with a negative $0.17 impact to Adjusted EPS<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">3</SUP>. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Outlook is provided in the context of greater than usual volatility as a result of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19</FONT> and
geopolitical uncertainty. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Conference Call </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International will host a conference call for investors with accompanying slides to review its results at 5 p.m. ET today. A
listen-only webcast will be provided at <U>www.mondelezinternational.com</U>. An archive of the webcast will be available on the company&#146;s web site. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>About Mondel&#275;z International </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (Nasdaq: MDLZ) empowers people to snack right in over 150 countries around the world. With 2021 net revenues
of approximately $29&nbsp;billion, MDLZ is leading the future of snacking with iconic global and local brands such as <I>Oreo</I>, <I>belVita</I> and <I>LU</I> biscuits; <I>Cadbury Dairy Milk</I>, <I>Milka</I> and <I>Toblerone</I> chocolate; <I>Sour
Patch Kids</I> candy and <I>Trident</I> gum. Mondel&#275;z International is a proud member of the Standard and Poor&#146;s 500, Nasdaq 100 and Dow Jones Sustainability Index. Visit <U>www.mondelezinternational.com</U> or follow the company on
Twitter at <U>www.twitter.com/MDLZ</U>. </P>

<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Additional Definitions </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Emerging markets
consist of the Latin America region in its entirety; the Asia, Middle East and Africa region excluding Australia, New Zealand and Japan; and the following countries from the Europe region: Russia, Ukraine, T&uuml;rkiye, Kazakhstan, Georgia, Poland,
Czech Republic, Slovak Republic, Hungary, Bulgaria, Romania, the Baltics and the East Adriatic countries. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Developed markets include the
entire North America region, the Europe region excluding the countries included in the emerging markets definition, and Australia, New Zealand and Japan from the Asia, Middle East and Africa region. </P>

program and the company&#146;s other transformation initiatives not yielding the anticipated benefits; changes in the assumptions on which the restructuring program is based; management of the company&#146;s workforce and shifts in labor
availability; consolidation of retail customers and competition with retailer and other economy brands; changes in the company&#146;s relationships with customers, suppliers or distributors; compliance with legal, regulatory, tax and benefit laws
and related changes, claims or actions; the impact of climate change on the company&#146;s supply chain and operations; strategic transactions; significant changes in valuation factors that may adversely affect the company&#146;s impairment testing
of goodwill and intangible assets; perceived or actual product quality issues or product recalls; failure to maintain effective internal control over financial reporting or disclosure controls and procedures; volatility of and access to capital or
other markets, the effectiveness of the company&#146;s cash management programs and its liquidity; pension costs; the expected discontinuance of London Interbank Offered Rates and transition to any other interest rate benchmark; and the
company&#146;s ability to protect its intellectual property and intangible assets. There may be other factors not presently known to the company or which the company currently considers to be immaterial that could cause its actual results to

<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:14pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. and Subsidiaries </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Reconciliation of GAAP and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Financial Measures </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>(Unaudited) </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company reports its
financial results in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States (&#147;GAAP&#148;). However, management believes that also presenting certain <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures
provides additional information to facilitate the comparison of the company&#146;s historical operating results and trends in its underlying operating results, and provides additional transparency on how the company evaluates its business.
Management uses these <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures in making financial, operating and planning decisions and in evaluating the company&#146;s performance. The company also believes that presenting these
measures allows investors to view its performance using the same measures that the company uses in evaluating its financial and business performance and trends. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company considers quantitative and qualitative factors in assessing whether to adjust for the impact of items that may be significant or that could affect
an understanding of its ongoing financial and business performance and trends. The adjustments generally fall within the following categories: acquisition&nbsp;&amp; divestiture activities, gains and losses on intangible asset sales and <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> impairments, major program restructuring activities, constant currency and related adjustments, major program financing and hedging activities and other major items affecting comparability of operating
results. See below for a description of adjustments to the company&#146;s U.S. GAAP financial measures included herein. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> information should be considered as supplemental in nature and is not meant to be considered in isolation or
as a substitute for the related financial information prepared in accordance with U.S. GAAP. In addition, the company&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures may not be the same as or comparable to similar <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures presented by other companies. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>DEFINITIONS OF THE COMPANY&#146;S
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">NON-GAAP</FONT> FINANCIAL MEASURES </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial
measures and corresponding metrics reflect how the company evaluates its operating results currently and provide improved comparability of operating results. As new events or circumstances arise, these definitions could change. When these
definitions change, the company provides the updated definitions and presents the related <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> historical results on a comparable basis. When items no longer impact the company&#146;s current or future
presentation of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> operating results, the company removes these items from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> definitions. In the first quarter of 2022, the company added to the <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> definitions the exclusion of incremental costs due to the war in Ukraine. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Organic Net Revenue&#148;</B> is defined as net revenues excluding the impacts of acquisitions,
divestitures and currency rate fluctuations. The company also evaluates Organic Net Revenue growth from emerging markets and developed markets. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Adjusted Gross Profit&#148;</B> is defined as gross profit excluding the impacts of the Simplify to Grow
Program; acquisition integration costs; the operating results of divestitures; <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity, forecasted currency and equity method investment
transaction derivative contracts; and incremental costs due to the war in Ukraine. The company also presents &#147;Adjusted Gross Profit margin,&#148; which is subject to the same adjustments as Adjusted Gross Profit. The company also evaluates
growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted Gross Profit on a constant currency basis. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Adjusted Operating Income&#148;</B> and <B>&#147;Adjusted Segment Operating Income&#148;</B> are defined
as operating income (or segment operating income) excluding the impacts of the items listed in the Adjusted Gross Profit definition as well as gains or losses (including <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> impairment charges) on
goodwill and intangible assets; divestiture or acquisition gains or losses, divestiture-related costs, acquisition-related costs, and acquisition integration costs and contingent consideration adjustments; remeasurement of net monetary position;
impacts from resolution of tax matters; impact from pension participation changes; and costs associated with the JDE Peet&#146;s transaction. The company also presents &#147;Adjusted Operating Income margin&#148; and &#147;Adjusted Segment Operating
Income margin,&#148; which are subject to the same adjustments as Adjusted Operating Income and Adjusted Segment Operating Income. The company also evaluates growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted Operating Income and Adjusted Segment Operating
Income on a constant currency basis. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
</DIV></Center>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Adjusted EPS&#148;</B> is defined as diluted EPS attributable to Mondel&#275;z International from
continuing operations excluding the impacts of the items listed in the Adjusted Operating Income definition, as well as losses on debt extinguishment and related expenses; gains or losses on interest rate swaps no longer designated as accounting
cash flow hedges due to changed financing and hedging plans; net earnings from divestitures; and initial impacts from enacted tax law changes; and gains or losses on equity method investment transactions. Similarly, within Adjusted EPS, the
company&#146;s equity method investment net earnings exclude its proportionate share of its investees&#146; significant operating and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-operating</FONT> items. The tax impact of each of the items excluded from the
company&#146;s GAAP results was computed based on the facts and tax assumptions associated with each item, and such impacts have also been excluded from Adjusted EPS. The company also evaluates growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted EPS on a constant
currency basis. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Free Cash Flow&#148;</B> is defined as net cash provided by operating activities less capital
expenditures. Free Cash Flow is the company&#146;s primary measure used to monitor its cash flow performance. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">See the attached
schedules for supplemental financial data and corresponding reconciliations of the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures referred to above to the most comparable GAAP financial measures for the three months ended
March&nbsp;31, 2022 and March&nbsp;31, 2021. See Items Impacting Comparability of Operating Results below for more information about the items referenced in these definitions that specifically impacted the company&#146;s results. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>SEGMENT OPERATING INCOME </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company uses segment
operating income to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. The company believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors analyze segment performance and trends. Segment operating income excludes unrealized gains and
losses on hedging activities (which are a component of cost of sales), general corporate expenses (which are a component of selling, general and administrative expenses), amortization of intangibles, gains and losses on divestitures and
acquisition-related costs (which are a component of selling, general and administrative expenses) in all periods presented. The company excludes these items from segment operating income in order to provide better transparency of its segment
operating results. Furthermore, the company centrally manages benefit plan <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-service</FONT> income and interest and other expense, net. Accordingly, the company does not present these items by segment because they
are excluded from the segment profitability measure that management reviews. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>ITEMS IMPACTING COMPARABILITY OF OPERATING RESULTS </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The following information is provided to give qualitative and quantitative information related to items impacting comparability of operating results. The
company identifies these based on how management views the company&#146;s business; makes financial, operating and planning decisions; and evaluates the company&#146;s ongoing performance. In addition, the company discloses the impact of changes in
currency exchange rates on the company&#146;s financial results in order to reflect results on a constant currency basis. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Divestitures,
Divestiture-related costs and Gains/(losses) on divestitures </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Divestitures include completed sales of businesses (including the partial or full
sale of an equity method investment - discussed separately below under the gains and losses on equity method investment transactions section) and exits of major product lines upon completion of a sale or licensing agreement. As the company records
its share of KDP and JDE Peet&#146;s ongoing earnings on a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-quarter</FONT> lag basis, any KDP or JDE Peet&#146;s ownership reductions are reflected as divestitures within the company&#146;s <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> results the following quarter. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Acquisitions, Acquisition-related costs and Acquisition integration costs </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On January&nbsp;3, 2022, the company acquired 100% of the equity of Chipita S.A. (&#147;Chipita&#148;), a leading croissants and baked snacks company in the
Central and Eastern European markets. The acquisition of Chipita offers a strategic complement to the company&#146;s existing portfolio and advances its strategy to become the global leader in broader snacking. The acquisition added incremental net
revenues of $152&nbsp;million and operating income of $4&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2022. The company incurred acquisition-related costs of $21&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2022. The company also
incurred acquisition integration costs of $35&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2022. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On April&nbsp;1, 2021, the company acquired
Gourmet Food Holdings Pty Ltd, a leading Australian food company in the premium biscuit and cracker category. The acquisition added incremental net revenues of $14&nbsp;million and operating income of $1&nbsp;million in the three months ended
March&nbsp;31, 2022. The company also incurred acquisition-related costs of $1&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On
March&nbsp;25, 2021, the company acquired a majority interest in Lion/Gemstone Topco Ltd (&#147;Grenade&#148;), a performance nutrition leader in the United Kingdom. The acquisition of Grenade expands the company&#146;s position into the premium
nutrition segment. The acquisition added incremental net revenues of $21&nbsp;million and operating income of $2&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2022. The company also incurred acquisition-related costs of $2&nbsp;million in
the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On January&nbsp;4, 2021, the company acquired the remaining 93% of equity of Hu Master Holdings, a category
leader in premium chocolate in the United States, which provides a strategic complement to the company&#146;s snacking portfolio in North America through growth opportunities in chocolate and other offerings in the well-being segment. As a result of
acquiring the remaining equity interest, the company consolidated the operation and recorded a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $9&nbsp;million ($7&nbsp;million <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax)</FONT> related to
stepping up the company&#146;s previously-held $8&nbsp;million (7%) investment to fair value. The company also incurred acquisition-related costs of $4&nbsp;million during the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On April&nbsp;1, 2020, the company acquired a majority interest in Give&nbsp;&amp; Go, a North American leader in fully-finished sweet baked goods and owner
of the famous <I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">two-bite</FONT></I><I><SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">&reg;</SUP></I> brand of brownies and the
<I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Create-A-Treat</FONT></FONT></I><I><SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">&reg;</SUP></I> brand, known for cookie and gingerbread house decorating kits. The acquisition of
Give&nbsp;&amp; Go provides access to the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">in-store</FONT> bakery channel and expands the company&#146;s position in broader snacking. The company incurred $1&nbsp;million of acquisition-integrations costs in the
three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Simplify to Grow Program </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The primary objective of the Simplify to Grow Program is to reduce the company&#146;s operating cost structure in both its supply chain and overhead costs. The
program covers severance as well as asset disposals and other manufacturing and procurement-related <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-time</FONT> costs. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Restructuring costs </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company recorded restructuring
charges of $11&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2022 and $88&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021 within asset impairment and exit costs and benefit plan <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-service</FONT>
income. These charges were for severance and related costs, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> asset write-downs (including accelerated depreciation and asset impairments) and other adjustments, including any gains on sale of
restructuring program assets. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Implementation costs </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Implementation costs primarily relate to reorganizing the company&#146;s operations and facilities in connection with its supply chain reinvention program and
other identified productivity and cost saving initiatives. The costs include incremental expenses related to the closure of facilities, costs to terminate certain contracts and the simplification of the company&#146;s information systems. The
company recorded implementation costs of $20&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2022 and $34&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021. </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Intangible asset impairment charges </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the first quarter of 2022, the company recorded a $78&nbsp;million intangible asset impairment charge in AMEA due to lower than expected growth and
profitability of a local biscuit brand sold in select markets in AMEA and Europe. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and currency derivative contracts
</I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company excludes unrealized gains and losses <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(mark-to-market</FONT></FONT>
impacts) from outstanding commodity and forecasted currency and equity method investment transaction derivative contracts from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> earnings measures. The <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts of commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives are excluded until such time that the related exposures impact the company&#146;s operating results. Since the company
purchases commodity and forecasted currency transaction contracts to mitigate price volatility primarily for inventory requirements in future periods, the company makes this adjustment to remove the volatility of these future inventory purchases on
current operating results to facilitate comparisons of its underlying operating performance across periods. The company excludes equity method investment derivative contract settlements as they represent protection of value for future divestitures.
The company recorded net unrealized gains on commodity, forecasted currency and equity method transaction derivatives of $28&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2022, and recorded net unrealized gains of $117&nbsp;million in the
three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Remeasurement of net monetary position </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the second quarter of 2018, primarily based on published estimates which indicated that Argentina&#146;s three-year cumulative inflation rate exceeded
100%, the company concluded that Argentina became a highly inflationary economy for accounting purposes. As of July&nbsp;1, 2018, the company began to apply highly inflationary accounting for its Argentinean subsidiaries and changed their functional
currency from the Argentinean peso to the U.S. dollar. On July&nbsp;1, 2018, both monetary and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-monetary</FONT> assets and liabilities denominated in Argentinian pesos were remeasured into U.S. dollars. As of each
subsequent balance sheet date, Argentinean peso denominated monetary assets and liabilities were remeasured into U.S. dollars using the exchange rate as of the balance sheet date, with remeasurement and other transaction gains and losses recorded in
net earnings. Within selling, general and administrative expenses, the company recorded remeasurement losses of $5&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2022 and $5&nbsp;million in the three months March&nbsp;31, 2021 related to the
revaluation of the Argentinean peso denominated net monetary position over these periods. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Impact from pension participation changes </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The impact from pension participation changes represent the charges incurred when employee groups are withdrawn from multiemployer pension plans and other
changes in employee group pension plan participation. The company excludes these charges from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> results because those amounts do not reflect the company&#146;s ongoing pension obligations. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On July&nbsp;11, 2019, the company received an undiscounted withdrawal liability assessment related to the company&#146;s complete </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">withdrawal from the Bakery and Confectionery Union and Industry International Pension Fund totaling $526&nbsp;million and requiring <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pro-rata</FONT> monthly payments over 20 years. The company began making monthly payments during the third quarter of 2019. In connection with the discounted long-term liability, the company recorded accreted interest of
$3&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2022 and $3&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021 within interest and other expense, net. As of March&nbsp;31, 2022, the remaining discounted withdrawal liability was
$356&nbsp;million, with $15&nbsp;million recorded in other current liabilities and $341&nbsp;million recorded in long-term other liabilities. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Incremental costs due to the war in Ukraine </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In
February 2022, Russia began a military invasion of Ukraine and the company closed its operations and facilities in Ukraine. In March 2022, the company&#146;s two Ukrainian manufacturing facilities in Trostyanets and Vyshhorod were significantly
damaged. During the first quarter of 2022, the company evaluated and impaired these and other assets. The company recorded $143&nbsp;million of total expenses ($145&nbsp;million <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax)</FONT> incurred as a direct
result of the war, including $75&nbsp;million recorded in asset impairment and exit costs, $44&nbsp;million in cost of sales and $24&nbsp;million in selling, general and administrative expenses. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Loss on debt extinguishment and related expenses </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On March&nbsp;18, 2022, the company completed an early redemption of long-term U.S. dollar ($987 million) denominated notes. The company recorded a
$129&nbsp;million loss on debt extinguishment and related expenses within interest and other expense, net, consisting of $38&nbsp;million paid in excess of carrying value of the debt and from recognizing unamortized discounts and deferred financing
costs in earnings and $91&nbsp;million in unamortized forward starting swap losses in earnings at the time of the debt extinguishment. </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On March&nbsp;31, 2021, the company completed an early redemption of euro (&#128;1,200 million) and U.S.
dollar ($992 million) denominated notes. The company recorded a $137&nbsp;million loss on debt extinguishment and related expenses within interest and other expense, net, consisting of $110&nbsp;million paid in excess of carrying value of the debt
and from recognizing unamortized discounts and deferred financing costs in earnings and $27&nbsp;million foreign currency derivative loss related to the redemption payment at the time of the debt extinguishment. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Initial impacts from enacted tax law changes </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The
company excludes initial impacts from enacted tax law changes from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures as they do not reflect its ongoing tax obligations under the enacted tax law changes. Initial impacts include
items such as the remeasurement of deferred tax balances and the transition tax from the 2017 U.S. tax reform. Previously, the company only excluded the initial impacts from more material tax reforms, specifically the impacts of the 2019 Swiss tax
reform and 2017 U.S. tax reform. To facilitate comparisons of its underlying operating results, the company has recast all historical <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP&nbsp;earnings</FONT> measures to exclude the&nbsp;initial impacts from
enacted tax law changes. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Gains and losses on equity method investment transactions </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Keurig Dr Pepper transactions </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On August&nbsp;2, 2021, the
company sold approximately $14.7&nbsp;million shares of KDP, which reduced its ownership interest by 1% to 5.3% of the total outstanding shares. The company received $500&nbsp;million of proceeds and recorded a
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $248&nbsp;million (or $189&nbsp;million <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax)</FONT> during the third quarter of 2021. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On June&nbsp;7, 2021, the company participated in a secondary offering of KDP shares and sold approximately 28.0&nbsp;million shares, which reduced its
ownership interest by 2% to 6.4% of the total outstanding shares. The company received $997&nbsp;million of proceeds and recorded a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $520&nbsp;million (or $392&nbsp;million <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax)</FONT> during the second quarter of 2021. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company considers these ownership reductions partial divestitures of
its equity method investment in KDP. Therefore, the company has removed the equity method investment net earnings related to the divested portion from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial results for Adjusted EPS for all
historical periods presented to facilitate comparison of results. The company&#146;s U.S. GAAP results, which include its equity method investment net earnings from KDP, did not change from what was previously reported. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Equity method investee items </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Within Adjusted EPS,
the company&#146;s equity method investment net earnings exclude its proportionate share of its equity method investees&#146; significant operating and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-operating</FONT> items, such as acquisition and
divestiture-related costs and restructuring program costs. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Constant currency </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Management evaluates the operating performance of the company and its international subsidiaries on a constant currency basis. The company determines its
constant currency operating results by dividing or multiplying, as appropriate, the current period local currency operating results by the currency exchange rates used to translate the company&#146;s financial statements in the comparable prior-year
period to determine what the current-period U.S. dollar operating results would have been if the currency exchange rate had not changed from the comparable prior-year period. </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>OUTLOOK </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company&#146;s outlook for 2022 Organic Net Revenue growth, Adjusted EPS growth on a constant currency basis and Free Cash Flow are <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures that exclude or otherwise adjust for items impacting comparability of financial results such as the impact of changes in currency exchange rates, restructuring activities, acquisitions
and divestitures. The company is not able to reconcile its projected Organic Net Revenue growth to its projected reported net revenue growth for the full-year 2022 because the company is unable to predict during this period the impact from potential
acquisitions or divestitures, as well as the impact of currency translation due to the unpredictability of future changes in currency exchange rates, which could be material as a significant portion of the company&#146;s operations are outside the
U.S. The company is not able to reconcile its projected Adjusted EPS growth on a constant currency basis to its projected reported diluted EPS growth for the full-year 2022 because the company is unable to predict during this period the timing of
its restructuring program costs, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivative contracts and impacts from potential acquisitions
or divestitures as well as the impact of currency translation due to the unpredictability of future changes in currency exchange rates, which could be material as a significant portion of the company&#146;s operations are outside the U.S. The
company is not able to reconcile its projected Free Cash Flow to its projected net cash from operating activities for the full-year 2022 because the company is unable to predict during this period the timing and amount of capital expenditures
impacting cash flow. Therefore, because of the uncertainty and variability of the nature and amount of future adjustments, which could be significant, the company is unable to provide a reconciliation of these measures without unreasonable effort.
</P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="right"><U>Schedule 8 </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. and Subsidiaries </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Reconciliation of GAAP to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Measures </B></P>

e.removeAttribute('id');a.parentNode.appendChild(e)}}
if(e)e.style.display='block';Show.LastAR=e};Show.hideAR=function(){Show.LastAR.style.display='none'};Show.toggleNext=function(a){var e=a;while(e.nodeName!='DIV')e=e.nextSibling;if(!e.style){}else if(!e.style.display){}else{var d,p_;if(e.style.display=='none'){d='block';p='-'}else{d='none';p='+'}
e.style.display=d;if(a.textContent){a.textContent=p+a.textContent.substring(1)}else{a.innerText=p+a.innerText.substring(1)}}}
